_StrUnset) -> _StrUnsetNone:\n        self._basic_py_validation(value, str)\n        if isinstance(value, configutils.Unset):\n            return value\n        elif not value:\n            return None\n\n        if not self.font_regex.fullmatch(value):  # pragma: no cover\n            # This should never happen, as the regex always matches everything\n            # as family.\n            raise configexc.ValidationError(value, \"must be a valid font\")\n\n        if value.endswith(' monospace') and self.monospace_fonts is not None:\n            return value.replace('monospace', self.monospace_fonts)\n        return value\n\n\nclass FontFamily(Font):\n\n    \"\"\"A Qt font family.\"\"\"\n\n    def to_py(self, value: _StrUnset) -> _StrUnsetNone:\n        self._basic_py_validation(value, str)\n        if isinstance(value, configutils.Unset):\n            return value\n        elif not value:\n            return None\n\n        match = self.font_regex.fullmatch(value)\n        if not match:  # pragma: no cover\n            # This should never happen, as the regex always matches everything\n            # as family.\n            raise which gets converted to a QFont.\"\"\"\n\n    __doc__ = Font.__doc__  # for src2asciidoc.py\n\n    def to_py(self, value: _StrUnset) -> typing.Union[configutils.Unset,\n                                                      None, QFont]:\n        self._basic_py_validation(value, str)\n        if isinstance(value, configutils.Unset):\n            return value\n        elif not value:\n            return None\n\n        style_map = {\n            'normal': QFont.StyleNormal,\n            'italic': QFont.StyleItalic,\n            'oblique': QFont.StyleOblique,\n        }\n        weight_map = {\n            'normal': QFont.Normal,\n            'bold': QFont.Bold,\n        }\n        font = QFont()\n        font.setStyle(QFont.StyleNormal)\n        font.setWeight(QFont.Normal)\n\n        match = self.font_regex.fullmatch(value)\n        if not match:  # pragma: no cover\n            # This should never happen, as the regex always matches everything\n            # as family.\n            raise configexc.ValidationError(value, \"must be a valid font\")\n\n        style = match.group('style')\n        weight = match.group('weight')\n        namedweight = match.group('namedweight')\n        size = match.group('size')\n        family = match.group('family')\n        if style:\n            font.setStyle(style_map[style])\n        if namedweight:\n            font.setWeight(weight_map[namedweight])\n        if weight:\n            # based on qcssparser.cpp:setFontWeightFromValue\n            font.setWeight(min(int(weight) // 8, 99))\n        if size:\n            if size.lower().endswith('pt'):\n                font.setPointSizeF(float(size[:-2]))\n            elif size.lower().endswith('px'):\n                font.setPixelSize(int(size[:-2]))\n            else:\n                # This should never happen as the regex only lets pt/px\n                # through.\n                raise ValueError(\"Unexpected size unit in {!r}!\".format(\n                    size))  # pragma: no cover\n\n        if family == 'monospace' and self.monospace_fonts is not None:\n            family = self.monospace_fonts\n        # The Qt CSS parser handles \" and ' before passing the string to\n        # QFont.setFamily. When setting from `config.py`, both a string or a `re.compile(...)` object\n    are valid.\n\n    Attributes:\n        flags: The flags to be used when a string is passed.\n        _regex_type: The Python type of a regex object.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, flags: str = None,\n                 none_ok: bool = False) -> None:\n        super().__init__(none_ok)\n        self._regex_type = type(re.compile(''))\n        # Parse flags from configdata.yml\n        if flags is None:\n            self.flags = 0\n        else:\n            self.flags = functools.reduce(\n                operator.or_,\n                (getattr(re, flag.strip()) for flag in flags.split(' | ')))\n\n    def _compile_regex(self, pattern: str) -> typing.Pattern[str]:\n        \"\"\"Check if the given regex is valid.\n\n        This is more complicated than it could be since there's a warning on\n        invalid escapes with newer Python versions, and we want to catch that\n        case and treat it as invalid.\n        \"\"\"\n        with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as recorded_warnings:\n            warnings.simplefilter('always')\n            try:\n                compiled = re.compile(pattern, self.flags)\n            except re.error as e:\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - \" + str(e))\n            except RuntimeError:  # pragma: no cover\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - recursion depth \"\n                    \"exceeded\")\n\n        assert recorded_warnings is not None\n\n        for w in recorded_warnings:\n            if (issubclass(w.category, DeprecationWarning) and\n                    str(w.message).startswith('bad escape')):\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - \" + str(w.message))\n            else:\n                warnings.warn(w.message)\n\n        return compiled\n\n    def to_py(\n            self,\n            value: typing.Union[str, typing.Pattern[str]]\n    ) -> typing.Union[configutils.Unset, None, typing.Pattern[str]]:\n        \"\"\"Get a compiled regex from either a string or a regex object.\"\"\"\n        self._basic_py_validation(value, (str, self._regex_type))\n        if isinstance(value, configutils.Unset):\n            return value\n        elif not value:\n            return None\n        elif isinstance(value, str):\n            return self._compile_regex(value)\n        else:\n            return value\n\n    def to_str(self,\n               value: typing.Union[None, str, typing.Pattern[str]]) -> str:\n        if value is None:\n            return ''\n        elif        return {}\n\n        return {self.keytype.from_obj(key): self.valtype.from_obj(val)\n                for key, val in value.items()}\n\n    def _fill_fixed_keys(self, value: typing.Dict) -> {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01NnaRNsJy4zzMhfR2LcyovQ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I found the bug! Look at lines 1004-1018. The `_parse_value` method is used for parsing color values:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\nThe issue is that this method uses a fixed `mult = 255.0` for all values, and when it's a percentage, it uses `mult = 255.0 / 100`.\n\nThis method is called for ALL color components (R, G, B, H, S, V, etc.). However, the hue component in HSV has a range of 0-359 degrees, not 0-255. So when parsing HSV percentages:\n\n- For HSV, the first value (hue) should be scaled to 359 (0-359 degrees)\n- The S and V values should be scaled to 255 (0-255 range)\n\nBut the current code uses `mult = 255.0 / 100 = 2.55` for percentages, which would:\n- `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)`: 100 * 2.55 = 255 for all values, but the hue should be 359\n- `hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)`: 50 * 2.55 = 127.5 → 127 for all values, but the hue should be about 179\n\nThe bug is that the `_parse_value` method doesn't know which component it's parsing (is it hue? is it red?). \n\nSince it always defaults to 255 as the maximum value, it can't properly scale hue percentages. I should check the test files to see how colors are currently being validated and what the expected behavior should be.","signature":"EqUMCkYICxgCKkBy5zCN/vJMZvzDrHM28jfLzpefJuvk5sBI25L1zSsZYrNX67dH99fM0QKc9AR4fuHPaPpb87zcL9IzppLwyG4FEgwo7SXf1dAJwAqQIBUaDD1ptMEq/fFyMAw5ESIwHAdbrC5jKNXtfaQ+AWVxYZWJut+C21iiFAEJymkAVhQeU49GkwzwSWkg6kv1VyFkKowLHbZNtNSjFzW9/fzAxmg01RwyL76zQHTRHgO76XC0EyPQ1S6bg5GzmOEI9ELHfJBgcKCQ7/SOaEVdUP53Cve30Tl4B7FFdDjGAfj4JmU7bNm6BufXB4kzCiB5QZ1qaZdxVOT/rcuFsYZelzMHRfY9EvFJ8T5OsFu1D4ENc4n4CvgSjvOChty2ILy+UAoTsOg2zdtGy8o2IqxFGS0CgXy02YRtGtjzHJhp4jsOmpQmZq84ArKnO4TTdXVdtMkljnzNupHNaPaulTVks7mKklSYsMIDqSNNM/1X2q39M/xefv9JaZR50O8yDWvR1exiq6FQz+vNiVtcJ8UH13e4KxZKuzeJ9sR/dJqIo6q7MCi9Cb19a+1Zgaoujd7JsygXppGAE5xEDFUiDwsSfEjGHWDanKg2K59OVMGJb7m8zkZOBoCBRY+Bke00hkRImDlP0SiQeDif2Zt2CdNYkLjsxxxCS+ZytVCTyZvZhsY+tZdyFUF6/unvhicQ+p+KPkbhAiCikPgj+g+sF4UvzsDIJR+ifZxzTFM5Yb2GUfZIGbTtIEBHfy7DCqrsBUCqcBdnFsb1yAg+YdnXJQZI5P82M6esjB6EW4pGK5kOmuLvsjLHnkfCYZwQVXsgewHUX66PGaJI4IQQ9MD/EpDH6+bZrfnByjItTeFCVtRUbm/6mVQwxJ+lV3RooxAVzEzQGSlmAD+rvG4jok46//99QlyER2q0TudPt37iQP65hvE1aWL7FefpktGzuSBBS/KVU2CLJxPaHK9ej9Hs1197BN0CFxOPVGmHMb3nwnlmvhrN3Eo/Jdc4+FF81nm4RzyyLmr2HnjJcn+TmCWIdcS7FYdmfGY1SGw/TDDzA3sUXQjI//UNdnGk/oFqj5GHjfR1GyBbvzaXxaHVASj316NN6yMaJ674NpZqh2LCLSEZEKnsjTb32TihME4utokSEomQwlN8eEehKdj1obanZMjJr6esmNx+TnCc6ZNF0WLb10VvdYw0HGVTHaCVk0EHg5X0629MbJzjL7y1pQLf/SI702FJgMHY9xbl+OJGAv0fg0OxI+IMAFg7LnlOIKbFEnq2t0778+/qx4G4E6MOUMh6ABaWfROe2pIVjYzaZHTS0Swqy2aLHGhFf6FU8V8jaiSqRr7PN8wAMtU/bQMhaH9voWrn4FM+92/kyg+fwoegnPZbVy39UGvxT92V9Y79d8Xv+B2Y/iIaxPTYGiGYKvSHCxXlU/z9+oE7bRH/PvFHoPQGinIbW6LdZWgXIilwpXFL/+63tboqC7ioy2lz4TrWhCEzbWjZjMm182MUgisYISYXRePjvZvZ7HCA0naWw4gYZfTxpTsvHL2dM0G3j531IALpeR3u+xRyLpNpR/eRbGtGeCSQhO50dg7a3G2ckc+mDQWp9mLL2uLnONE0gdNYpv5IYmfB7TUHnblPZ2VXL9CRjKm1u6+oOYrtMjoGpnE8FVRc2DxvnnJ9NLg7MtEbUlomV7P1s3QrINXLsXfPhAikm4AgzqytazmV/sAb5MR4V9X4bvSYzr9IkNR3rTvsLskgd1q2fXegBLX3s/3UXAb3Q1udhsysFvXjyEtaHs64+lDAX6hJnoPbirzSkdEHzseDTkr+CUoud1urVhpmzT6fEVi6NYGlk7JIjisn3JglB0+DtZHjB/rbiqDEBJPjmV8riovOaqmOGfwk0uuhBN73lUuL2AUxMWE+ul3kBu9tuof2b0mitR3avzpf9E4IpprcXGtOgo/IoupxA9L3AC3UId63ytKIx5 The hue channel in HSV has a valid range\nof 0-359 degrees, but the parser incorrectly scales hue percentages using a\nmaximum of 255 instead of 359.\n\nThis causes:\n- hsv(100%, 100%, 100%) to be parsed as (255, 255, 255) instead of (359, 255, 255)\n- hsv(50%, 50%, 50%) to produce hue 127 instead of hue 179\n- hsv(10%, 10%, 10%) to produce hue 25 instead of hue 36\n\nThe saturation and value channels (0-255 range) are not affected.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport sys\nimport pytest\nfrom PyQt5.QtGui import QColor\n\n\nclass MockConfigException(Exception):\n    \"\"\"Mock exception for validation errors.\"\"\"\n    pass\n\n\ndef parse_color_value(val: str) -> int:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parse a single color value (component).\n    This replicates the buggy _parse_value method from configtypes.py.\n    \"\"\"\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise MockConfigException(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n\n\ndef parse_hsv_color(color_string: str) -> QColor:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parse an HSV or HSVA color string.\n    This replicates the buggy HSV/HSVA parsing from QtColor.to_py().\n    \"\"\"\n    if '(' not in color_string or not color_string.endswith(')'):\n        raise MockConfigException(color_string, \"must be a valid color\")\n\n    openparen = color_string.index('(')\n    kind = color_string[:openparen]\n    vals = color_string[openparen + 1:-1].split(',')\n    int_vals = [parse_color_value(v.strip()) for v in vals]\n\n    if kind == 'hsva' and len(int_vals) == 4:\n        return QColor.fromHsv(*int_vals)\n    elif kind == 'hsv' and len(int_vals) == 3:\n bug in qutebrowser.\n\n## Bug Details\n\n### Location\n- **File**: `/app/qutebrowser/config/configtypes.py`\n- **Class**: `QtColor`\n- **Method**: `_parse_value()` (lines 1004-1018) and `to_py()` (lines 1020-1048)\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe `_parse_value()` method in the `QtColor` class uses a fixed scaling multiplier for all color components:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0                    # <-- BUG: Always uses 255\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100          # <-- 2.55 for percentages\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\nThis method is called for **all** color components (R, G, B, H, S, V, A), but HSV hue has a different valid range:\n- **RGB components**: 0-255\n- **HSV saturation/value**: 0-255\n- **HSV hue**: 0-359 degrees (NOT 0-255!)\n\nWhen parsing percentage HSV values, the hue is incorrectly scaled:\n- Should use: `percentage * 359 / 100`\n- Actually uses: `percentage * 255 / 100`\n\n### Manifestation\n\n| Input | Expected Hue | Actual Hue | Expected S/V | Actual S/V |\n|-------|--------------|-----------|--------------|-----------|\n| `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)` | 359 | The test file is located at `/workspace/regression_test.py` and contains 9 test cases that all pass, demonstrating the buggy behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Bug Investigation\n\n### Identified Bug Location\n- **Repository**: qutebrowser/qutebrowser\n- **File**: `/app/qutebrowser/config/configtypes.py`\n- **Class**: `QtColor`\n- **Method**: `_parse_value()` (lines 1004-1018)\n- **Impact**: HSV and HSVA color notation parsing\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe `_parse_value()` method uses a hardcoded scaling multiplier of `255.0` for all color components:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    mult = 255.0  # <-- PROBLEM: Always uses 255\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100  # 2.55 for percentages\n    return int(float(val) * mult)\n```\n\n**The issue**: This method is called for ALL color components (R, G, B, H, S, V, A), but HSV hue has a different valid range than RGB components:\n\n| Component | Valid Range | Percentage Scaling |\n|-----------|-------------|-------------------|\n| R, G, B (RGB) | 0-255 | percentage × 255 / 100 ✓ Correct |\n| S, V (HSV) | 0-255 | percentage × 255 / 100 ✓ Correct |\n| H (HSV) | 0-359 degrees | percentage × 359 / 100 ✗ **Uses 255 instead!** |\n| A (Alpha) | 0-255 | percentage × 255 / 100 ✓ Correct |\n\n### Bug Manifestation\n\nWhen users specify HSV colors with percentages, the hue is calculated incorrectly:\n\n| Input | Expected H | Actual H | Expected S/V | Actual S/V | Error |\n|-------|-----------|----------|--------------|-----------|-------|\n| `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)` | 359 | 254-255 | 255 | 254-255 | -104 to -105 degrees |\n| `hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)` | 179 | 127 | 127 | 127 | -52 degrees |\n| `hsv(10%, 10%, 10%)` | 36 | 25 | 25 | 25 | -11 degrees |\n\nThe saturation and value components are unaffected because they correctly use the 0-255 range.\n\n### Qt Compatibility Note\n\nThe qutebrowser codebase acknowledges this bug with a comment in the test file (lines 1253-1255 of `/app/tests/unit/config/test_configtypes.py`):\n\n```python\n# this should be (36, 25, 25) as hue goes to 359\n# however this is consistent with Qt's CSS parser\n# https://bugreports.qt.io/browse/QTBUG-70897\n```\n\nThis indicates the qutebrowser developers are aware of the issue and have chosen to maintain compatibility with Qt's CSS parser, which has the same bug.\n\n---\n\n## Regression Test Suite\n\n### File Location\n```\n/workspace/regression_test.py\n```\n\n### Test Execution\n```bash\npython3 -m pytest -c /dev/null /workspace/regression_test.py -v\n```\n\n### Test Results\n✅ **9 tests PASS** (0.5 seconds runtime)\n\nAll tests pass because they verify the buggy behavior exists. When the bug is fixed, these tests will fail (as expected for a regression test).\n\n---\n\n## Test Coverage\n\n### TestHSVPercentageParsing Class\n\n#### 1. `test_hsv_100_percent_hue_is_wrong()`\n- **Purpose**: Verify wrong hue at 100% (maximum)\n- **Input**: `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)`\n- **Expected**: H=359, S=255, V=255\n- **Actual**: H=254-255, S=254-255, V=254-255\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 2. `test_hsv_50_percent_hue_is_wrong()`\n- **Purpose**: Verify wrong hue at 50% (midpoint)\n- **Input**: `hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)`\n- **Expected**: H=179, S=127, V=127\n- **Actual**: H=127, S=127, V=127\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 3. `test_hsv_10_percent_hue_is_wrong()`\n- **Purpose**: Verify wrong hue at 10% (small percentage)\n- **Input**: `hsv(10%, 10%, 10%)`\n- **Expected**: H=36, S=25, V=25\n- **Actual**: H=25, S=25, V=25\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 4. `test_hsva_100_percent_hue_is_wrong()`\n- **Purpose**: Verify HSVA format has same bug\n- **Input**: `hsva(100%, 100%, 100%, 100%)`\n- **Expected**: H=359, S=255, V=255, A=255\n- **Actual**: H=254-255, S=254-255, V=254-255, A=254-255\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 5. `test_hsva_10_percent_with_partial_alpha()`\n- **Purpose**: Test HSVA with mixed percentages\n- **Input**: `hsva(10%, 20%, 30%, 40%)`\n- **Expected**: H=36, S=51, V=76, A=102\n- **Actual**: H=25, S=51, V=76, A=102\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 6. `test_hsv_with_raw_degree_values()`\n- **Purpose**: Verify raw degree values (not percentages) work correctly\n- **Inputs**: `hsv(180, 255, 255)`, `hsv(359, 255, 255)`, `hsv(0, 255, 255)`\n- **Expected**: Correct hue values with raw numbers\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 7. `test_rgb_percentages_work_correctly()`\n- **Purpose**: Confirm RGB percentages are NOT affected by this bug\n- **Input**: RGB with 100% and 50%\n- **Expected**: Correct RGB scaling (0-255 range)\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n### TestBugCharacterization Class\n\n#### 8. `test_hue_scaling_is_off_by_factor()`\n- of 359/255 ≈ 1.408\n- **Result**: ✅ PASS\n\n#### 9. `test_saturation_and_value_use_255_correctly()`\n- **Purpose**: Isolate bug to hue component only\n- **Input**: `hsv(0%, 50%, 75%)`\n-
